SAMOANS MAY
BE ONCE MORE
PLUNGED IN WAR
Mataafa and Malietoa
Ready to Fight.
RUNAWAY CASHIER CAUGHT
TAKEN OFF STEAMER MARI-
POSA AT AUCKLAND.
Sophia Peterson, a IT-Year-Old Girl,
Wants to Die Because Jack En-
nis, a Pugilist, De
serted Her.
The Oceanic Steamship Company's mall
steamer Marlposa arrived from Sydney, N.
S. W., via Auckland, N. Z.. Apia, Samoa,
and Honolulu, Hawaiian islands, yester
day. During the last three days of the
run very heavy weather was encountered,
the wind veering from southeast to west
northwest with startling rapidity. Last
Tuesday morning at 1:30 o'clock It was
blowing- from the south-southeast, when
without a moment's warning a violent
squall came down from the west-north
west. The steamer sustained no damage
and came along at her nsual speed, ar
riving on time. She brought over $1,250,
--000 In treasure, being the balance of trade
between the colonies and America,
The officers f the Mariposa do not be
lieve the cablegram from Sydney, N. S.
W., which says that Mataafa has been
elected King of Samoa.
"The steamer Janiuni, which carried the
news to New Zealand, left Apia the day
befora we did," said Captain Hayward
yesterday. "On her way to Auckland she
had to call at Tonga and would about
reach New Zealand the time the cable-
gram was sent. Now, when we left Sa
moa no King had been made. Both Ma
taufa and Malletoa claimed to have been
elected and the Chief Justice was to give
a decision three or four days after we
left.
"Whichever way the decision went
trouble was expected, as the followers of
each candidate vowed they would tight
if the other chief was made King. In
anticipation of trouble United States Con
sul General Osborn and British Consul
Maxse had given notice that 'the persons
of the Chief Justice and of his family and
his private residence, as well as the Su
preme Court, are under the protection of
the American and British flags and any
attack on them will be considered an at
tack on the flags."
"Tl*; natives were coming Into Apia by
the thousands while the Mariposa lay
there. Mataafa has a following of about
16,0w) warriors, while Malietoa has only
about 5000. They were all killing pigs and
laying in stores of provisions a-s well .is
furbishing up their weapons and getting
ready for a fight. The British man-of
war Ringdove and the German gunboat
Bussard were in port and ready for an
emergency. When we were there it
looked very much as though there would
be fighting over the kingship before it
was all over and done with."
Among the passengers who left Sydney,
N. S. \V., for San Francisco on the Mari
posa were a "William Hudson" and a
"Mrs. Mary Rodgers and three children."
When the vessel reached Auckland, N. Z.,
detectives went aboard searching for a
Frank Butler, wife and three children.
Butler was a clerk in the employ of the
Carrington Coal Co-operative Shipping
Company, Newcastle, N. S. W., and ab
sconded with $1875. Hudson and Mrs.
Rodgers answered the description of Mr.
and Mrs. Butler, and they were arrested.
No money was found on Hudson, but in
a strong box Mrs. Rodgers had $450 in
English gold, $450 In English silver and
?200 in American money. Hudson was
detained, but Mrs. Rodgers was released
and came on to San Francisco. She says
Hudson was only a friend of hers and was
taking care of her on the steamer, as she
was not a very good sailor.
Passengers for Honolulu by the mall
steamer Australia had a lively time of it
leaving port yesterday. The bar was
breaking, and the stout vessel wa3 buried
again and again in the breakers. After
crossing out, however, it was all plain
sailing, and Captain Houdlette laid his
course for the islands.
The steamer Colon arrived from Pan
ama and way ports yesterday. At Aca
pulco she picked up Captain "Pete" Ott,
the pilot v. ho was carried away on the
City of Para.
The water front will be in a pretty bad
way after the storm. The blow came
when unusually high tides were the order
of the day, and in consequence all the
illling 4n has been washed away. There
are a number of dangerous holes near the
Harbor Receiving Hospital, the ap
proaches to the Broadway wharves are
in a bad condition and section 3 of the
seawall is once more in need of repair.
Down at Spear street the buildings will
begin to slip into the bay if something be
not done soon. Over in Oakland Creek
the Afon Alaw ran amuck, and on this
side the City of Dawson broke adrift
again. The Afon Alaw got alongside the
Santa Clara, and after doing considerable
damage to her started on another cruise
and ran into the ship Bohemia. She was
finally moored in a place where- Bhe could
do no damage.
Sophia Peterson, a girl 17 years old, and
living at 119% Kearny street, attempted
to commit suicide yesterday. She Is in
love with a pugilist named Jack Ennis,
and when he told her he was going away
she took a dose of oil of almonds. At the
Harbor Hospital Dr. Fltzglbbon pumped
her out, and she is now on the road to re
covery.

Adopted.
At a special meeting of the Board of Su
pervisors held last night to consider the
proposition of holding an exposition in
j this city in 1901, It was the unanimous
sentiment of the members that the pro
ject was in every way worthy of their
support. The committee of fifteen ap
pointed by Mayor Phelan to take the af
fair in hand was present, and through
Charles Bundsehu. Richard P. Doolan, A.
S. Baldwin, President A. A. Watkins of
the Board of Trade, S. H. Friedlander
and General Warfleld, as spokesmen, re
quested the board to pass resolutions ask
ing the Legislature for the power to ap
propriate $1,000,000 for exposition purposes,
the committee then to request the Legis
lature for a special State appropriation of
$250,000, and a further national Congres
sional appropriation of &00.000.
A letter was read from J. B. Reinsteln,
chairman of the committee, in which he
1 made a strong plea for the moral and
i physical support of the Supervisors. While
; the latter were inclined to lend their aid
they were In doubt as to what plan would
be the more feasible, a tax levy covering
a period of three years or an issue of
bonds for the required amount. Tn either
case it would be necessarry to have an
enabling act passed by the Legislature
giving them authority in the premises.
On motion of Supervisor Perrault the
rooms of the board were placed at the
disposal of the committee on plans for
the exposition, which will meet on Sat
' urday at 3 p. m.. when the matter will be
j further discussed and a definite plan of
action decided on.
It was stated that a subcommittee of
three, consisting of W. 11. Mills, Charles
Hundschu and A. A. Watkins, had com
municated with the various commercial,
industrial, banking and other organiza
tions of this city, requesting each of them
! to appoint a committee of three, which
will be added to the original committee of
fifteen, and will raise the number of tne
latter to 150 members. This general com
mittee will meet the Mayor, Auditor and
the Board of Supervisors on Saturday,
< when the best plan to insure the success
! of the exposition will be adopted.
Cut by an Angered Husband.
While trying to save a woman from
being brutally beaten by her husband last
night. John Jones of 413 Clemontlna street
1 wns severely cut about the face and head
; with the jagged end of a broken bottle
wielded by the enraged man. The trouble
occurred in the house adjoining the one
occupied by Jones. He says that the man
who Injured him is named Kelly. Jones
was taken to the Receiving Hospital,
where the injuries were dressed by Dr.
Tormoy. His assailant was arrested.
Ireland and Its Scenery.
Rev. Eugene Sheeny of Limerick, Ire
land, lectured last night at Metropolitan
Temple. He took for his subject "Ireland,
Its Architecture, Its History- and Its
Scenery." His remarks were Illustrated
by a magnificent collection of views
shown through a stereopticon. The
speaker was frequently interrupted by ap
plause by those in the audience, many of
whom seemed familiar with the route
taken. The lecture will be repeated to
night.
An Evening With Bangs.
The entertainment given last evening !n
the Y. M. C. A. Auditorium for the benefit
of the Children's Home Finding Society
was both an artistic and a financial suc
cess. The little hall was crowded. The
main feature of the entertainment was
the classical, humorous and sentimental
recitations of D. C. Bangs, the well
known impersonator.
Bay View School Affairs.
Henry All wood, vice president of the
Bay View Improvement Club, asks that
a mlsstatement regarding the distance
between the Burnett School and the Bay
View School be corrected. It Is about a
mile and a half, while the types some
days since made it only half a mile. The
number of pupils, according to Mr. All
wood, will be about fifty-five.
Death of Mrs. Mortenson.
BERKELEY, Jan. 11.â Mrs. Henrietta
F. Mortenson died last night at Fablola
Plospital as the result of a surgical opera
tion. The body was removed to-day to
the residence on Woolsey street, Lorln,
from where the funeral will be held to
morrow afternoon at 2 o'clock.
He Pleaded Guilty.
J. E. Gilligan, the young man who tried
to swindle several miners and was nearly
lynched for his attempt, pleaded guilty
In Judge Conlan's court yesterday. He
will appear for sentence this morning.
